=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 5
Not at all a fan, but rating a 5 because it's a functional game and might be a fun solo. Played twice. In the second game, one player with slight input figured out the strategy for victory, laid out the plan, and then we just spent all game executing it without any real decision-making. Nothing came up to really derail us, despite some monster spawns.  By the time we reached the boss we had to take down in the scenario (not mentioning  which one to avoid spoilers),  we were all so well-prepared that despite his best double-six rolls, he died in a single turn. One major issue with the game was the huge downtimes. Sometimes it was very advantageous to have one character waste all their moves on one very short task. After that, the player had nothing to do  for the whole scenario. As a result, players who had finished until the next day would go chat with friends, leading them to not be involved in the big decision-making. By the time they returned, the strategy was fully laid out and their move was already optimized. Sometimes people chose to do something suboptimal  just for fun, but it's annoying to me when a game makes it so clear what the optimal moves are. I felt the game was playing us rather than us playing the game. Moves are tight in the game and the right move is clear, so it's impossible for alpha gamer types to not dominate. Overall - I can't say I had a bad time playing this game, but compared to the ambiguity of games like Pandemic or the hidden information  of games like Dead of Winter, I doubt I could justify actually playing this game again, unless I was playing solo. And frankly, there's better, less-fiddly solo games out there.

RATING: 7.5
I think for an easy to get into fantasy, this is the best way to do it. For balance, it swings alot. It starts off deceptively easy - too easy in fact. And then after a legend or two, you get dumped into the deep end of the pool. The game at that point becomes a stressful puzzle requiring repeated plays to solve. Not sure how many times I'm willing to do that. Such a technique works in a computer game, but given the over all set up and play time, not sure in a board game. Still, I like it and would like to see the expansions in English (I'm certain I'm not alone in that).

EDIT: I did eventually solve all of it. It *was* purely a puzzle in the end - once you find the solution, the game is tense, but mechanical. It truly needs expansions to keep it alive, but I find my interest is waning in the view of other fantasy romps heading to my collection soon.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
I played this game only three times, so these are mostly impressions that may change after multiple plays.

I've strong mixed feelings about Legends of Andor. The first time I played it I was really disappointed, because I was expecting a very different game. I felt the mechanism of the storyteller to be restrictive and annoying, because I wanted to kill monsters freely instead. Starting from my second play I approached it as a puzzle to be solved instead of an "hack and slash"-kind of game and I liked it much more... but still felt kinda limited by the rules of the game.

There are many reasons to like this game. First of all the artwork is among the most beautiful I've ever seen. The board is full of tiny interesting details, that really make the game come to life, and it's maybe the thing I like the most about Legends of Andor. At the same time the game presents itself pretty well also mechanic-wise, as the turns flow smooth and without much downtime. It's also interesting to see a fantasy adventure game with such strong euro-mechanisms combined with a strong narrative frame. For sure this hybridization is part of the game's success, as it appeals to different kinds of players.

Yet, as far as I'm concerned, I liked the game but not as much as I wanted to like it. I felt restricted by its mechanisms, because there's always a few moves that you HAVE TO take during the course of the game and I don't like the fact that basically the game is forcing me to make a specific choice. It's really a pity though, because I've been searching for a good cooperative game for quite some time and I thought this could be one that would fit my taste. Maybe that's why I've such strong mixed feelings... because I see what this game could have been for me, if only a few mechanisms would have been different. That's why, even if I enjoy it and I recognize that it's a good game, this seems like a negative review, even if the rating is positive.

I wanted to love this game, but I expected something different from it. I still like it, I would gladly play it again... but I can't help being a little upset for a few mechanisms, that significantly reduced my enjoyment. Good game, but arghhh!

RATING: 5
Many co-ops feel like you are completely at the luck of the draw. This means winning or losing feels like its determined by a shuffle. Legends of Andor didn't feel that way at all. The story is driven by the cards and the gameplay is very smooth. Did not feel clunky the way many coops do. 

Bonus points for the way the game is learned, I hope more games adopt the tutorial mode approach.

RATING: 9
Pros:
+ Brain-burner adventure
+ Beautiful art, really impressive
+ Very nice narrative
+ Overall good quality components
+ Somewhat fast game (1 to 2 hours)
+ Very enjoyable as solo or co-op
+ Simple rules; excellent rules book; excellent learn as you play system

Cons:
- Bad English and Portuguese translations; there are errors in game components that interfere with game play
- Low replayability; requires new legends to maintain interest

Neutral:
+- Cards are on the cheap side
+- Creatures AI is predictable but that is what drive the puzzle aspect of the game

Verdict:
* Fascinating; one of the best fantasy/adventure games ever created

RATING: 7
как сразу же заметила Л., сюжет всё-таки ощутимо обогащает игровой процесс. кампания состоит из пяти связанных друг с другом сценариев, шестой автор предлагает придумать самим (даже вложил пустые карточки). 

сама игра - не вполне традиционное фентези. оно с первого взгляда может показаться америтрешем, но на самом деле это скорее головоломка. кубики играют куда меньшую роль, чем в "Аркхэме", а каждый убитый враг передвигает фишку рассказчика (= кладёт жетон безысходности, ускоряя пробуждение Древнего). т.е. тут нужно именно выполнить задания сценария, а биться только по острой необходимости. автор, кстати, адресовал данную "проблему" в первом же большом дополнении к игре ("Легенда вторая: Поход на Север") - там рассказчика двигает только каждый второй (а позже третий) трупик.

другая любопытная деталь - я не уверен, что вчетвером играть проще. город тогда нужно оборонять куда тщательней, а прямая выгода от четырёх героев - лишь в битве (ну и ходить можно в разные места, возможно в других сценариях это будет важно).

(ожидал, что примерно такой игрой будет "Властелин колец" Книции)

воин и маг решают.

Лида после четвёртой легенды: "Хорошая игра, есть ощущение, что голова постоянно работает, а не просто следит глазами за некими действиями, с плохо обусловленным выбором между ними".

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
Pretty fun. I was expecting it to be sort of like Pandemic, but with more theme and story, and I would probably say that's a fairly accurate description.

Unlike Pandemic, there's collaboration right off the bat. Everyone has to work together as a team, not just haphazardly run around clearing up cubes. And, since you need to split your attention between multiple goals, there's a lot more strategy of deciding how to balance your play. And despite all of this, it's still a fairly straightforward game to learn. You move or fight. If you move, you get to do the whatever at the place you stop.

So I definitely like it better than Pandemic as a game.

But, on the other hand, it's really a bear to set up. Besides going through checklists of components to hunt down and allocate, you also have to deal with the haphazard arrangement of numbers on the board when placing things. Of the 90 minute playtime, you could easily spend 20 minutes doing setup. If you're just planning to play once and then tear it down, it's probably not worth it. I'd suggest passing on this one unless you can set it up and leave it out on a table for a week or two while you play through the campaign.

And as to the campaign, I have so far only played the tutorial (Legend 1) and Legend 2. And, in both, the real engine of the game is killing monsters that are encroaching on the castle. I'm not sure how the other map works (on the backside of the board), but I'll be a bit disappointed if every Legend amounts to playing the tower defense style game, while running a few mini-missions to the side. And, unfortunately, that's really how the "story" felt in the game. While you will often get 2-3 (tarot card sized) pages per chapter of the Legend, the story blurbs are probably less than 20% of the total text and most of the rest of it is new numbers to find and put monsters on, for the tower defense game.

Given the still rather slight quantity of story in the game, the sheer quantity of little chits seems excessive.

So...I like it as a cooperative. I'd appreciate the thematic elements more if I could leave all the chits out and not have to clean up and set back up each time I play. But as a game to take to meetups, this one is probably not going to see much light. It doesn't tell a good enough story to make it worth the hassle.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 6
 Καθαρά συνεργατικό fantasy παιχνίδι όπου οι παίκτες σε ρόλο ηρώων προσπαθούν να φέρουν εις πέρας αποστολές ενώ παράλληλα προστατεύουν το βασίλειο από επιθέσεις ορκ. Κλασσικό theme αλλά αυτό δεν είναι απαραίτητα κακό.
	
Το παιχνίδι αντί για μινιατούρες χρησιμοποιεί χάρτινα stand-ups. Τα τόκενς είναι καλοφτιαγμένα και το artwork είναι εξαιρετικό (εγγύηση ο Menzel) οπότε δεν με ενόχλησε καθόλου η απουσία μινιατούρων. Οι ήρωες γενικά προχωράν στο χάρτη, σκοτώνουν τέρατα και υπάρχουν κάποια σημεία που αλληλεπιδρούν με το ταμπλό. Κάνουν Level up και αγοράζουν εξοπλισμό.  Να σημειωθεί πως το ταμπλό είναι διπλής όψεως με άλλες περιοχές στη πίσω πλευρά.

Περιέχονται 4-5 πίστες οι οποίες συνδέονται σεναριακά κάτι σαν ψευτό-campaign δηλαδή. Η κάθε πίστα έχει συγκεκριμένα events που συμβαίνουν σε προκαθορισμένα χρονικά διαστήματα και προωθούν την ιστορία. Εδώ βρίσκεται και το πρώτο πρόβλημα του παιχνιδιού καθώς ναι μεν η όλη φάση έχει πολύ ενδιαφέρον την πρώτη φορά που παίζεις την πίστα αλλά από την άλλη άπαξ και ξέρεις τι πρόκειται να συμβεί τότε χάνεται η μαγεία και αρχίζεις να  προσπαθείς να τρέξεις ή να καθυστερήσεις το επόμενο event. Με λίγα λόγια οι πίστες πάσχουν από replayability.

Το άλλο που δεν μου έκατσε καλά είναι το γεγονός πως ο χρόνος τρέχει κάθε φορά που σκοτώνεις κάποιο τέρας και επειδή ο χρόνος γενικά είναι λίγος πρέπει να σκεφτείς πόσα και ποιά τέρατα πρέπει να σκοτώσεις. Προσωπικά βρίσκω αντι-θεματικό το ότι το παιχνίδι σε τιμωρεί αν σκοτώσεις πολλά τέρατα. Τι σούπερ ουάου ήρωες είμαστε αν αφήνουμε επιλεκτικά τέρατα να μπουν στην πρωτεύουσα??  

Τα όποια μειονεκτήματα του παιχνιδιού πιστεύω πως λύνονται με 1-2 expansions και το καλό είναι πως το παιχνίδι είναι φτιαγμένο έτσι που να είναι εύκολα expandable. Αν δεν θέλετε να μπείτε στον κόπο μπορείτε να παίξετε μια φορά όλες τις πίστες για την εμπειρία και μετά να το δώσετε για ανταλλαγή.

RATING: 6.5
Michael Menzel is one of the most renowned artists in the boardgame industry, and I am a big fan. When I heard about his first design, and about all the marketing Kosmos put in place for it... I was intrigued a lot!

The game itself is a coop adventure, where the german school of design intrudes in a field that's normally the domain of ameritrash: mechanics are simple and elegant, and dice rolls can be mitigated in various ways.

The game's aesthetics are obviously top tier, and the absence of plastic miniatures is barely noticeable, thanks to the wonderful stand ups Menzel drew.

The game itself contains five different Legends (or quests), and only the first couple (designed as tutorials) are not replayable: the others have an amount of random elements and can be replayed at will.

Definitely a good game, that deserves its prizes!

RATING: 6
For the most part, I enjoyed the plays I had.
My main drawbacks are the puzzle-feeling and that the story-chapters have only limited replay value.
Especially towards the end of the game it turned into a puzzle for me. One session I was able to prove that we have no chance at winning 4 turns before the game regularly ended :(
And if you know the story of a given chapter you already know what will happen and can therefore prepare and don't get caught on the wrong foot.
The 2 drawbacks add to each other – the more I know what will happen, the sooner I leave the fantasy-realm and begin to start to view it as an abstract, a puzzle.

Now my comment sounds more negative than it's meant to be :)
I enjoyed playing the game, but be wary that you may only have quite a limited amount of plays in the box (bang for your buck).

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 6
Con [url=http://ballearicus.blogspot.com.es/2013/07/resena-n-22-las-leyendas-de-andor.html#more]Las leyendas de Andor[/url] estemos posiblemente ante un juego que no encaja con ninguno de los lectores de esta reseña (yo incluido), pero que nosotros no somos su público objetivo, somos el hilo conductor. Jugado en mi grupo habitual, Las Leyendas de Andor no pasaría el corte de la segunda leyenda (la primera no cuenta, es un tutorial) y se iría directo al fondo de la estantería, al mercadillo o a la mastrade, pero con mi crío esto cambia, la liga en que juega es otra, su baremo es otro. El que suscribe vive con intensidad y al unísono las aventuras a través de sus ojos, de su perspectiva, con su percepción de lo que acontece, donde cada combate, cada lanzamiento de dados, cada lectura de carta, cada evento y contratiempo es una nueva sensación para él y a mi, me recuerda lo que sentía cuando a su edad, jugaba con mi hermano al Heroquest.

La excitación de la planificación del turno, diciendo cosas como “… papa, no te preocupes, de éste que me encargo yo, porque mi guerrero puede lanzar cuatro dados. Después con el oro, me voy al mercader a subir mi fuerza”. Llevo cuatro partidas en una semana (él ya está de vacaciones), no hace mas que pedirme otra y presiento que estoy ante un juego incombustible, ya que no le importa repetir escenarios (hemos hecho dos veces las dos primeras leyendas para consolidar conceptos) aunque sepa que es lo que va a salir.

Y es que el germen ha sido plantado. Antes de encarar el reto de la destrucción del anillo único en “La guerra del anillo” o evitar que despierte el primigenio en una lejana ciudad de Massachuset en “Arkham Horror”, tenemos vivir, sufrir y prepararnos en “Las Leyendas de Andor”.

RATING: 9
Wonderful co-op puzzle that not only rewards coordinating actions, but often requires full collaboration (as in, players fighting together in the same battle). The scenarios are challenging enough that you don't often win your first time, but you have a better chance the second time around. There is a problem with knowing what is coming, though, which takes some of the fun out of it. Since we don't plan on playing this dozens of times a year, the lack of replayability isn't a problem for us (we usually forget what happened in a scenario when the game hits the table again). 

However, why oh why hasn't FFG agreed to support the expansions?!? And for a Spiel des Jahres nominee for that matter! If there's any game that absolutely would benefit from expansions (e.g. adding replayability with different maps/scenarios), it's this game. Because it's so language dependent, an English edition is a must. Fantasy Flight, come on!!

UPDATE: Yay! Kosmos to the rescue!

I do think my rating will go up when I get to play it with my “real” friends and family, as that’s where cooperative games really shine I think.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 6
My score for this game has gone steadily downward. The mechanics are simple, the graphics are great, the components are of good quality and the fact each character is playable as a male or female version complete with its corresponding figurine is simply awesome.

However, that is where the positives end, in my opinion. The set-up is quite elaborate and differs for every legend/scenario. The game is scripted, which feels like railroading. Also, since not all the information is out in the open at the start of the scenario and the scenario cards are only revealed during play, the odds can change unexpectedly during the first play of a scenario. During subsequent plays, the element of surprise is not that big. This means the game rewards experienced players and becomes less replayable over time. I find myself dreading new scenario card reveals, as they more often than not result in more bad stuff for the players.

In short, my gripe is that everything is either scripted and bad for the players OR entirely random. The game feels very unfair and does not allow for anyone going about their own business to even the slightest extent.

RATING: 4
I see the same main problem with this game as many of the other people who commented:
I find it utterly idiotic that the legend marker which makes you loose when it reaches the end advances for defeating monsters. Sure, fighting monsters takes time, but that is not reflected by the legend marker, it is already reflected by advancing your time marker one hour for each round of battle. If running through the forest for an hour doesn't advance the legend marker, then fighting a monster for an hour shouldn't, either.
I don't find thematic storytelling issues too important for most other games, but the very strength of this type of game should be that it tells an interesting and most of all comprehensible story about the actions of your heros as the main characters. It feels completely unheroic and illogical to have to meticulously plan if you can afford to kill another monster who wants to kill the women and children in the castle you are defending because that would cause a mysterious out-of-story storyteller to accelerate time or tell your legend faster or whatever and thus make you loose.
If there was some in-story justification for having to avoid fights such as "these monsters aren't really evil, just misguided, so you need to absolutely make sure to not kill a single one more than you have to", that could be OK I guess. Or much better, one could fix another illogical weakness of the game by making loosing against monsters have more severe consequences (short of killing the hero because player elimination sucks). That would also give the players an incentive to think about which fights they pick, if that is what the designer wants.
But no effort whatsoever seems to have been made to provide a logical in-game explanation consisent with the story that is told for why defeating monsters makes you loose.

I have only played the first introductory legend once and thus can't yet rate the stuff that gets added in the other legends, but the problem above was so off-putting for me that I didn't have much incentive to play it again.
If I still do anyway, I might change my rating a little (up or down), but I doubt it'll increase appreciably.

Other issues I have with the game are the inherent follow-the-leader tendency and the very limited replayability.

All in all, this is *by far* the most disappointing Kennerspiel des Jahres for me. Well, actually, it is the only disappointing Kennerspiel des Jahres so far, I love 7 Wonders and like Village and Istanbul.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

RATING: N/A

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7.7
I kind of have a love/hate relationship with this game. I think it's a fantastic game for the most part. The artwork is gorgeous, and I love the gameplay, quests, and combat. It's just really demoralizing and so very frustrating when you lose, but it's glorious when you win. The game just isn't very forgiving at all. Kill just one too many monsters or the wrong monster early in the game, and it can be the difference between winning and losing.

The game doesn't scale very well to the number of players. Legend 2 is easier with 4 players and too difficult with 2 players, but Legend 3 is too difficult with 4 players. In Legend 3, more players means more Fate cards to resolve before you can fight the final Big Bad, and that takes more time and you can only let one monster into the castle before it is overrun. Fate cards which take farmers out of the game are the worst, especially in a 4-player game.

I think the tutorial in Legend 1 is actually very innovative, but I do wish there was a more conventional rule book to go with it. When you need a clarification on some rule, it can be hard to find the rule because all the rules are spread out between the the tutorial, the Standard Setup Legend cards, various other Legend cards, the Battle board, the Merchant board, etc. There's the 4-page rules summary which attempts to bring everything together, but it's missing a bunch of rules in my experience.

RATING: 9

Only three plays in as I write this, but it's clear that Legends of Andor is an amazing design that will both frustrate and delight all at once.

Bought this to play with my wife and nephew. All of us were super exited after barely solving the first Legend.

And then we experienced Legend 2.

It's interesting to note everyone's experience: I became practically obsessed in trying to solve the "puzzle" ... but my wife and nephew wanted to dumb down the game in order to win after getting frustrated at the difficulty.

To me, LOA is quite the litmus test; I look forward to playing this with others to see what happens.

Update: Still can't crack Legend 2 after five attempts -- I'm clearly stupid -- but I think I see a path for success now.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 10
Players represent heroes, summoned to Andor to protect the kingdom.  Cooperative fantasy game, told in story/event format.  Players have 7 hours in the day to take actions around the land, and may "exert" themselves to take three more hours.  Players may attack monsters roaming the land, but with the caveat they are accelerating the story which may bring on more monsters, and hasten the end of the game.  The plot advances with a deck of legend cards, which bring on monsters, give the heroes quests, and tick things over.  Monsters move in regular fashion, advancing from space to space, but always edging closer to the castle (and player defeat).  Combat is almost pure Talisman, roll some dice and add strength.  Really well designed game, with some nice ideas, great way of presenting the rules, and looks stunningly beautiful.  Five legends to play, double sided game board, tons of bits in the box, really low entry cost - you could sit down and play this with grandma.  Descent has been bumped - this is so much nicer to play, and offers a good thinky challenge.  Excellent.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

RATING: 9
We started to play and were fascinated by this game. Yesterday we played it three times in a row and finally defeated the black dragon.

What I really love about the game:

+ It is really storytelling
+ Every time it plays differently
+ The artwork is great
+ It is a fantasy game but with lighter theme
+ Although there are random factors in the game, it is necessary to plan and possible to win by good gameplay
+ It sometimes feels like a riddle how and when each character should act
+ Just by killing monsters as much as you can will lead to your defeat
+ The game has kind of an AI, so that the monsters appear and move "by themselves" (but of course the game itself can not really "react" or change its strategy in order to deal with the actions of the heroes. Nevertheless the heroes actions trigger meaningfull events)So sometimes it feels like playing a videogame (in a good sense)

I think it is a perfect blend of an american- and eurostyle type of game and it definitely opens a new era of boardgaming!

RATING: 4
Legends of Andor is a beautiful game. Legends of Andor is a challenging game. Legends of Andor is not a fun game.

I was expecting a co-op adventure game. In reality, Legends of Andor is a demanding puzzle game. You must intricately manage your resources and actions to prevent the monsters from overrunning the kingdom.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
Fun cooperative fantasy game. It's more "cooperative" than "fantasy" though. So games don't last for hours and your job isn't to clear the board and eradicate loads of critters, but to pick and fight strategic battles to steal victory from the evil forces. There are no fancy armors and weapons, but the items you do have feel really powerful. Every fight pushes the clock forward and there is so much to do and so little time.

Even though there are no miniatures and they use cardboard standups, they are still gorgeous and can hold their own. They are painted from the front and back, so there is still a three-simendional quality to them when you see them on the board. The two-sided board is also beautifully drawn and shows a wide range of different landscapes. The only drawback is that the numbers on the spaces don't seem to follow any particular order so searching for a specific number can be slightly annoying.

Storydriven coop adventure game with a very euroish feel, which might be a turnoff for those who are expecting a little bit more chaos and less puzzling. I really like the low-fantasy art in this game, and the fact that the male and female versions of each character look almost identical to the point that it is hard to tell them apart (this is really (and sadly) not the case with most adventure games).

The first scenario is a tutorial and should be regarded as such. The real game starts with the second scenario and then takes off fully with scenario 3 that offers true replayability through the random quests and setup. And scenario 4 has it's own mapboard!

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 9
This is a game unlike any other I have experienced. Posing as your classical high-fantasy RPG/dungeon crawler, this is actually a very thematic and immersive coop puzzle adventure game. Even while including many of the genre's tropes, the realm of Andor feels fresh, vibrant, and ripe for adventure. The board is the most gorgeous I have ever seen, and it is double-sided! All the other components are just as beautiful, perfectly marrying functionality and aesthetics.

Kudos to Menzel for the learn-as-you-play approach: you can basically start playing after reading a simple one-page introduction to the rules. There are no mechanisms to counter quarterbacking, though, but it is otherwise a top-notch co-op experience. Just don't expect the game to be focused on combat, as its core is instead both the puzzle-y coordination of each hero's actions and the unraveling of the story itself. After the third scenario I decided I wanted to get the expansions, and even the website has plenty of extra content to download. Couldn't be more pleasantly surprised!

RATING: 8
Initial rating after playing one legend.

This game is fun but it is presented in an odd way. The rules change for the scenario and then change again during the scenario and the rules are presented in little bite sized pieces.

RATING: 8
Not quite what you'd expect - this is not a fantasy adventure where you merrily go around, slay monsters and pick up treasure. Instead Legends of Andor is a fantasy-themed puzzle game where you try to figure out a way to solve the adventure with a limited amount of moves. It's unusual, but works beautifully. There is also enough randomness to ensure decent replayability: you can easily play each of the 6 legends through 2-4 times with different characters - and 15-20 plays is pretty good replayability for any game in my book.

Works also very well as a solo game.

RATING: 6
Once you figure out how to play (worst rulebook ever), it's actually pretty smooth and enjoyable.  We really liked it, but I'm wondering about replayability.

UPDATE: I've tried to bring this game out on several occasions, but it's always with a new group, so I have to repeat Legend 1.  One time I tried starting new players in Legend 2 and there's just too much fussing around and they get lost right away, not understanding how the game mechanics flow together and the time track.  Given that I don't have a regular game group that is willing to learn and focus on this game and work through the missions, I decided I'm going to put it up for trade / sale, but not before my wife and I play through the 4 missions.

We got the game out tonight and I couldn't help but be annoyed at the setup... every time we pull this thing out it takes 20 minutes to read through all the setup.  We chose Legend 3, as both of us have completed Legends 1 and 2.  We probably made it 3 turns in and were both so annoyed at how fiddly everything is and how often I had to refer back to the rules to find out what herbs cost (oh, everything costs $2, okay), or that this guy moves twice, but not before this other guy moves, and what happens if I die in battle again?  There's just so much re-looking rules up that it pulls me out of the story constantly, and storytelling is supposed to be the game's strong suit.  It's just not for us.  Game is in perfect condition, all the parts are counted and bagged and ready for a new home.  If my son was 10 or 12 and wanted to play through this with me on summer vacation, I'd keep it.  But he's 2.  :P

RATING: N/A

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 9.5
From the very best boardgame artist comes the best cooperative game I have ever played. One thing I really like is that there is a story that develops as you play, and it goes on across the various "legends" (scenarios). The potential for creating custom scenarios with your own stories is fantastic!

The mechanics are relatively simple and generally intuitive. The exception to the latter, of course, is that killing monsters advances the time counter. It works as a rule, but it is absolutely unthematic and sometimes a bit annoying. It adds to the feeling of solving a puzzle that the game provokes, which is not what people expect from adventure games. That is probably not a bad thing, as I'm so often disappointed by adventure games and enjoy this one.

A minor complaint: the need to defend the castle often causes the two-player game to devolve into one player taking this task and the other doing all the rest. Another problem is that there are too few scenarios (the alternate side of the board is only used by one of them) and expansions will be necessary to increase the game's longevity. But I would certainly buy them, anyway.

On the production, my only gripe is the choice of cardboard standups instead of plastic miniatures for the heroes and monsters. But that is comprehensible, given the designer's background as an artist. And being Michael Menzel's artwork on those standups surely reduces my discontentment.

I can't finish, however, without commenting on the presentation of the rules. It does not affect my rating, but the learn-as-you-play novelty, with essential rules on cards and the lack of a conventional rulebook, was a terrible idea. I like to read and learn all the rules before I can teach the game, not to mention to look them up if necessary, and this approach makes that impossible. To add insult to injury, the introductory scenario treats the players like morons, with the simplest of rules (such as flipping a token when you enter its space) written on tiles scattered across the board. I'm glad that Kosmos already recognized the mistake and made available an "extended rulebook", but this should have been in the box.

RATING: 7
Legends of Andor is a puzzle/co-op game, set in a Fantasy setting, and featuring not only the wonderful art of Michael Menzel, but his game design as well.

The game sets players up against measured threats, and limits their choices by scenario- sometimes the straightforward hack your way through method is not the best choice, and heroes may run out of time and lives trying to win by brute force.

After a 2-player play of the first scenario, I found it reasonably challenging, and it certainly dropped a surprise or two during the game play.

I am starting this Kennerspiel des Jahres Winner at a 7; if the next scenarios prove a bit more replayable I will be still more pleased.

On the whole this was a nice surprise for me.

RATING: 10

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8.5
Wow! Simply put, one of the best games I have played. I'm kicking myself for not owning it back when it came out, but at the same time ecstatic, because I purchased at the best time. Under the FFG brand , aka the "Ameritrash-expansion-dice-central" of the board game world, Legends of Andor got absolutely no love. It won the Kennerspiel 2013 but FFG was too busy milking out Arkham Horror expansions to give two turds about a sleeper hit they had on their hands. It seemed like many of its fans in North America, would never see any expansions/love to this game. 

Thankfully KOSMOS decided to do the English translation themselves and now many expansions, that the German market have been enjoying will see North American shores. The game has a strong Fantasy feel, almost Lords of the Rings-ish" as you and your partners work together to take on different Legends. The game has all the markings of a typical "Descent-style" fantasy but it is an entirely different beast altogether. The game is indeed more Euro, and scenarios are presented in more of a puzzle, that players have to solve to have a favorable outcome. Going full spartan mode, and charging and killing all your enemies costs you time and resources, and if you attempt it as so, you will quickly find yourselves losing. 

The game is definitely more brain than brawn, and that's why I love it. It has simple combat with dice mechanics, but the meat of the game is finding out the best course of action to take with your adventurers, each of which plays differently, to complete each scenario. The game ships with five scenarios, a few of which have variable setups. I own the Star shield expansion as well, which adds one new scenario with 6 different possible endings.

RATING: 6
Large Tolkien-style fantasy cooperative game, where you are fighting off waves of baddies to save the castle, all while completing side quests to further the story or get bonuses to help you.

You and your allies must move around the board, with a limited number of actions per day to use each.  At the end of each day, there may be some advancement of the story but there is always an event card which makes at least something happen.

The game definitely encourages cooperation and planning, you stand a much better chance against the enemies if you fight together, and you often need to take items across the board in tandem.  Also the spoils of victory can be distributed as you please, so this allows for more discussion and general collaboration.

I have only played 2 of the base game Legends so far, but both have been OK and I imagine that the other ones are more of the same.  My only complaints with this game really are that it seems to be relatively easy, and that the theme is completely generic and indistinguishable from other fantasy universes of its ilk.  A fun game though, and actually plays fairly quickly despite it's size and number of components.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

RATING: 7
Very nice first outing for MM as designer here. Similar to Robinson in many ways (less the theme), which speaks well for it in my eyes. 

Robinson is the deeper more involved game with tougher decisions, this one is MUCH easier to learn and also easier play, but its definitely not all fluff like some have passed it off as, not at all and decisions are not [i]all[/i] obvious here, to put it in perspective Robinson is probably the deepest co-op on the market as of 2012, and I would say decisions are a little more thought provoking here than Pandemic. Pandemic and this (or even more so DOTR) also share some things so its another apt comparison. 

Both Robby and this have significant setup time as a negative, but LoA has VERY elegant rules overall, top marks for this, gameplay is pretty streamlined, not checking the rules every couple of turns like Robby... I think the story element comes through maybe a touch more in Robby, compared to others in the genre I would say LoA does quite well here also though, both are thick in theme but don't expect a Dungeon Crawl here, its not. 

The timer moving against you when you kill a Monster is kinda anti-thematic, depending on how you look at it, easy to see why he did it and not a deal-breaker for most I would think. Minis should would have been nice (and another scenario or two, replay suspect for sure)! Make sure you play past scenario one which is just a learning game.

RATING: 8.2
Bokkensprong 18/12/2015. Coöperatief avonturenspel, kruising tussen Hero Quest, Risk,... De helden krijgen een opdracht die ze moeten vervullen per legende. Per beurt kan je een van beide acties doen: verplaatsen of vechten. Elke actie kost een uur op de tijdschaal; na zeven uur is de dag om en bewegen de monsters richting kasteel. Wordt het kasteel ingenomen, dan verliezen de helden. Vechten = dobbelen met x dobbelstenen, waarvan enkel de hoogste telt, en er je kracht bij optellen. Dit wordt vergeleken met het resultaat van de monsters; het verschil in score wordt afgetrokken van de wilskracht van de verliezer. Het volgende uur gaat de strijd zo verder. Monsters die op nul staan, zijn verslagen en leveren een beloning op; de legendemarker gaat daardoor echter ook wel vooruit.
Niet evident met vier; zeer moeilijk te winnen met twee! Lukt beter met wat ervaring.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
Fun, tense, puzzly co-op. I was convinced for most of the game that we had no chance, but the way that the game developed it ended up working out. It stacks things pretty heavily against you and it doesn't let up but it gives you opportunities to improve your situation and deal with ever escalating threats. It reminded me a bit of Robinson Crusoe in that way where you can be a bit proactive, as opposed to something like Pandemic which to me feels very reactive. I really liked how you can't just kill every monster you see because that will push up the time track and finish the game before you've accomplished all of the objectives. But at the same time the monsters are a very real threat and not killing the right ones will very quickly lose you the game. So you have to be very selective in which fights you take. Each adventurer also feels unique and fits the class they're supposed to be. Overall the theme came through pretty well for me.

RATING: 8.5
Mechanically simple when seen from a "gamers" point of view. But there's a lot to like in Andor: The scripted legends really make you feel that you're taking part in a proper story, rather than just running around bashing monsters. The components are great and of course the artwork is fantastic. My 8-year old son loves it. :)

The "turn marker" advances when you kill something" controversy is a non-issue for me, the trick is not to see it as a measure of time spent, but as an abstract "how far along in the adventure are we" marker - and progress in the adventure in this game mainly depends on the number of monsters killed.

With only five scenarios, one could worry about replayability, so here's hoping for lots and lots of expansions!

But for now we are enjoying this immensely! Excellent game, highly recommended.

RATING: 6
2015-09-22

Initial Rating: 6.5 (September 2015)

For some reason I didn’t want to play Legends of Andor, perhaps because it is a CoOp game and most games in this category have disappointed me. However I found myself in an uncommon situation, we were two players and only had games for three or more players so we had to play Legends of Andor or go home. Now I’m glad I did as the game surprised me.

The rules are pretty easy, but the decisions aren’t in any way obvious, Legends of Andor is a challenging game (as a good CoOp should be). There is some luck but you can mitigate it with clever play (group combat) or buying upgrades. I like how you spend “time” to get things done.

The game components are ok but the game art is very good. It also tells a good story, that is, it has a good theme that is in congruence with the game mechanisms. 

I think it is best with 4 players (although I haven’t played in that configuration).

What I really like about the game, is that the gameplay feels really different from most CoOps I have played, the reason is that you cannot kill monsters just because, as in most games (I always do that as I’m generally the tank). In Andor every time you kill a monster, the timer advances so you really have to think your moves/kills through. I’m impressed by this because it really adds a new dimension to the game (however this doesn’t make thematic sense to me and this is a minor flaw because the game is supposed to be thematic).

On the bad side, I’m not sure about the game replayability. Once I have successfully completed a legend, there is very little motivation for me to revisit it. I also would have loved that the legends were interconnected, but as I understood the game, each legend is independent (other than for storytelling purposes). 

Bottom line, I enjoy Legends of Andor and I’m open to playing all the legends, however, I think I won’t buy it because I feel the game has a very low replay value for me. Perhaps it is too simple for my current tastes.

Current Rating: 6.0

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 5
I went into this with high hopes as an adventure game that I could play at equal footing with the kids (12 and 7). In that very specific goal, it somewhat succeeds. For some, I believe that is enough. For me, it turns out, it isn't. 

First off, the 14+ age on the box is a total joke. This is a 10+ game, and playable down to age 7 with some help. In fact, there is not enough tension or interesting decisions in this game to make it anything other than a game you play with your kids. I can't imagine sitting around a table of adults to play this.

My caveat is that I only played the first three legends, but I have no interest in going further. 

What did I like? I do like the fact I can play it with my kids. I think that the mechanics are smooth and make sense.

What do I feel ambivalent about? The game pieces out the rules to you in the legends as you play them. This gets you playing fast, but also leaves you too much in the dark about why it is you are even playing the game. For those who are not used to playing gamer games or learning from rulebooks, it's probably good. For those of us who eat rule books for breakfast, it gives you the sense of feeling around in the dark and is frustrating. A rule book, called a "reference book" is included, but you almost feel guilty reading it, as if it is going to give away some great reveal that will come in a later legend. This style of game teaching is certainly not for me, but it isn't necessarily a bad thing.

What don't I like? The first two legends were WAY too easy. I gave the first one a pass for being an intro, but we won the second legend with 3 days to spare. That is a lot of time! In both legends we defeated the enemies in one day and had two days or so with nothing to do before the next legend card introduced anything new. It is easy to gain strength and willpower and very hard to lose it. While I appreciate that the events are not too powerful and random, they have so little impact as to be practically meaningless. 

Never in our games did anybody feel threatened by anything. Our decisions were obvious, once the game decided to let us know what to do. Even if future legends get harder, which I am sure they do, I don't see much room for the game to get any more interesting. With only 5 legends in the box, replayability would appear to be a major, major issue as well. I could never imagine wanting to play any of these again after playing them through once.

A really big miss, in my opinion, is the story aspect, which should be this game's core strength. I found nothing to care about in the story. No real characters. The legend cards had two sentences of story and 3 paragraphs of instructions. Nothing about them felt legendary in any way!

What did my kids think? (Maybe that is the most important aspect here?) They didn't dislike it, but neither did they ask to play it again. I had to make strong suggestions to get them to do Legend 2. If my kids fell in love, that would be enough for me to call this a sure keeper. But that didn't happen.

Outside of having an adventure game that you can play at equal footing with your kids, I can't see anything much to recommend this game. And honestly, my kids get far more excited about playing the venerable Mystic Wood than Legends of Andor!

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 9
Chez nous le jeu est un grand succès avec les enfants qui en redemandent! Par contre il faut savoir que ce n'est pas un "hack and slash", il ne faut pas s'attendre à tuer tous les monstres et ramasser plein de trésors et monter de niveau. Pour cela je regarderais plutôt un jeu comme Heroquest ou Heroscape. Andor est un casse-tête avec un thème d'aventure très bien senti. La gestion du temps provoque un sentiment de stress qui immerse totalement les enfants (pleurs de défaite et cris de victoire, pipis en urgence parce qu'ils se retiennent pour ne rien manquer). C'est un des jeux où la collaboration est vraiment nécessaire, si un joueur fait un tour sans considérer les autres ça met tout le monde en péril.

Un conseil essentiel pour réussir les missions: il ne faut pas essayer de battre les monstres avec juste un personnage, il faut toujours se mettre au moins deux, même pour les monstres les moins forts. On sauve énormément de temps de cette façon.

La puissance des scénarios varie avec le nombre de joueurs, on peut jouer de 2 à 4, et aussi à 2 avec 2 personnages chacun, ce n'est pas difficile à gérer. J'ai une préférence pour 3 ou 4 personnages à la fois.

Nous jouons avec les enfants, mais le niveau de difficulté est élevé, il faut un peu d'aide des adultes pour encadrer les décisions (sans que l'on joue à leur place non plus)

RATING: 7
Cooperative storytelling in a light manner. Players can play as one of four different classes with a male/female counterpart for each class. The game ships with 6 legends. I have only played 3 so far, however, what I have played has not been insanely challenging. The formula works, however, as players spend time collecting resources, increasing their strength, and waging battle against four different monster types: Gor, Skraal, Troll, and Wardrak, with extra additional bad guys in the game. If you enjoy dungeon delving and story telling this is a pretty good and thematic game. I'm not sure on replayability, and I think the game suffers because of it. This game should be an 8, but from what I played it seems like there isn't enough to continually play it. Hopefully more content is released with additional legends, but I'm sure it will be costly. As it is a solid 7.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

My husbands and my favorite game to play together.  Great challenging co-op that also gives a little bit of a dungeon crawl feel but works really well for 2 players.

Legends of Andor is a cooperative adventure board game for two to four players in which a band of heroes must work together to defend a fantasy realm from invading hordes. To secure Andor's borders, the heroes will embark on dangerous quests over the course of five unique scenarios (as well as a final scenario created by the players themselves). But as the clever game system keeps monsters on the march toward the castle, the players must balance their priorities carefully.

RATING: N/A
Dario
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
This is definitely a more puzzle-based adventure where time management is key rather than say a dungeon crawl. The action points causing some people to have fewer turns per day than other people feels a bit odd but since days are generally pretty short anyways it's not a huge deal. Combat feels like a good balance of not being predetermined and yet not being too luck-based, and I like how the heroes use their dice in combat differently, although team battle seems really strong.

The basic mechanics of this game are pretty simple. Teaching the game via a tutorial legend was a little bit strange, and I feel like telling me all the rules that are used in the first legend right off the bat in a normal rule book format would have been easier than walking me through different parts as the legend progressed. I did like how the tutorial legend took out some of the extra-detail rules though, as I foresee it making this game a lot easier to teach to nongamers.

I've seen some comments of people saying they didn't like this game because you want to avoid killing stuff as much as possible. While it is true that you can purposely let a couple of monsters slip past, you still have to kill the majority of monsters and/or rush to the end condition quickly, and so combat is still very important, you just have to fight in a time-efficient manner. 

There are some very thematic little quirks in this game that makes it feel like it is going the extra mile. For example, there is an event card that causes a howling wind to hurt everyone in spaces 1-20. Seemingly random within this region of the board is a space numbered in the 70's, but on this space there is a picture of a house, indicating you weathered the storm by taking shelter.

The story in the legends while not having a huge amount of flavor text is cohesive and at least in my limited plays so far makes each legend feel unique. Setup time is a bit long.

Haven't played the last legend yet, but of the first 4 the game is pretty easy, which is probably its biggest flaw (barring a special surprise in one of the legend 3 final encounters). While Legend 4's setup looks initially impossible it actually isn't too bad. Legend 3 and 4 feel very different and since 3 plays differently every time, it adds a lot of variety to the game, although I think for the most part it dwarfs Legend 2. While I am disappointed that this game isn't smacking me in the face with difficulty every time I still have a blast playing it, and for that alone have to give it a solid 8.

EDIT: Well I did finish all the legends a long time ago, but realized recently I had been playing the advance the legend track after defeating a monster wrong. While I feared this lack of integration of game balance with thematic sense would be really bad, aftwr playing it again the fact you still have to kill a decent number of stuff makes me not dislike it that much, and I definitely like that the game is more difficult with the correct rules.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

RATING: 6
Coops are not my thing, so it is debatable how much sense it makes for me to rate them. Nevertheless, I can appreciate good stuff even in games that I'm not that much interested in myself. And what strikes me the most about Andor is how obviously it is a labor of love.

And if you're a brilliant game illustrator, making a game your labor of love will be quite visible, of course, but there is a lot of ideas and detail packed into the game itself, too. The impact that bloodshed has on the game clock is one example of that, forcing you to carefully weigh when and which opponents to kill.

I've only played the first two legends so far, and I'd not be averse to try the 2nd one again, or delve deeper into the Legends of Andor. Which, from me, is high praise for a coop game, so if you like that kind of gaming, this is definitely recommended.

RATING: 6
Legends of Andor is a fantasy based co-op game with a euro bent.  In it players are trying to defend the castle of Andor from hoards of invading creatures, while also attempting to complete side missions.

The game is very innovative in that it is episode based, and the episodes teach you the game as you go.  In particular episode one, or rather legend one, teaches placement of pieces out on the board, and how they are used, etc.  Another innovation is that the game uses two time tracks.  One track shows you how much time you have left in a day, or round.  The other one shows how many rounds are left before the game ends.  It's this second track that posses a great problem for players.  You see, as the monsters steadily march toward the castle only a small number can get in before the castle is overrun.  If it is ever overrun the players lose.  So, you must kill monsters off.  However, every time you kill a monster it advances the round track, leaving players with fewer rounds to accomplish their goals.  So, when it comes to killing monsters you're damned if you do, and damned if you don't.  This aspect of the game makes Legends of Andor very difficult to win.  The game is essentially a giant moving puzzle where players must work against time, and space, to do all the things they need to do.

Legends of Andor sports maybe the most beautiful game board ever created.  It is a sprawling vista of the land of Andor - on one side.  The other side depicts the underground caves that exist beneath the mountains.  All the pieces, in fact, are very well rendered.

I like Legends of Andor.  I wish I loved it, but I don't.  It all comes down to that round track.  I feel like the game is cheating me.  I have no choice but to kill monsters to protect the castle, but every time I do the game takes another round away from me in which to complete my mission(s).  Bad form, I say.  Bad form.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 3
Based on the first scenario ("legend"), this is so random it hurts (and I normally do not mind random). I think the main reason I detest it here is almost the same story will unfold. You see, on one hand this tries to be a story-driven game with randomized combat, on the other hand it wants to be a (hard, it seems) euro-inspired puzzle. That does not mix well.
And to make it worse it does not scale well to 2 players. At least not in the first scenario.

The worst part though is, at the middle of the scenario something happens in the story which changes the win/loose criterias. So I have to adapt, but at this point it was clear that the scenario is unwinnable based due to my previous choices *which were made without this knowledge*. So the only way I can win this is to replay, having knowledge about how the story will unfold. This, to me, is a major design flaw. If they want to make a changing story I should not have to know what will happen in order to win.

And what is up with the abstraction? Whenever I win a battle against a create I have 1 less day to complete my mission. Really? So, just to be clear, character A is running all he can in the east trying to deliver a message, hoping character B, who is in the west, will not battle a creature, thus depriving him of important running time. Yeah, that does not make sense.

If I want a fantasy game I will prefer to look elsewhere (although there is too far between good coop fantasy games), and if I prefer a puzzle I can definitely find it elsewhere. All in all this is a title to avoid for me.

RATING: 7
[microbadge=1714]

[u]21-May-2013[/u]:  I probably shouldn't rate this one yet as I've only played the first Legend so far, but I really liked what I saw.  This is another one of my co-op games that I'll probably play only solo.  You are a group of standard fantasy heroes who must complete Legend specific quests before the Castle is overrun by monsters or the time track reaches its end.

There is combat in the game, but the main focus is the questing.  And I like that.  I've got Gears of War and Death Angel for combat games.  I wanted an adventure game, and I think this is a good one.  Again, I've only played the basic / learning Legend so far.  I am assuming things will only go up from here.

Oh, and the components are fantastic.  The artwork is beautiful.  Especially the double sided board.  It comes with cardboard standies, but I don't find them a problem in the least.  And, you can play the male or female version of your character...a nice touch indeed.

I'll probably have more to say after I get more into this one, but at this point, I'd say this is a great adventure game.

[u]24-Jan-2014[/u]:  Well, I finally played the second scenario...once.  I think this game is pretty sweet.  It's an adventure quest game with a good narrative feel to it.  Not having a traditional rulebook, I think, is what holds this game back for most people.  And that's a shame.  It's really fun and puzzle-y and beautiful to look at.

After two solo plays and two co-ops, this is definitely a game that CAN suffer to the quarterback (it is very puzzle'y).  That said, there is the possibility that it can be overcome by not thinking about it too much or not allowing others to tell the current player what to do

In any event, it is a good game that I think is fun to play through as many Legends as possible due to the story, but it isn't something that you would want to replay

Other issues the game has is the high luck factor, with the outcome of battle being decided on dice (with some mitigation when performing a team battle or with high strength) or the draw of event cards

RATING: 8
What a strange game. Even after reading multiple reviews of it the first game defied expectation. At its heart Andor is a solid if traditional co-op experience. It's the extra stuff that draws me in as a player- the small exploration aspect of the fog, the paper-doll inventory, the steady alterations to narrative and mechanics that happen as a result of the legend cards. Not to mention the weird obsession with wells. This one went from trade-bait to trying to track down the German expansions in four games. A keeper.

RATING: 7.5
Die Legenden von Andor ist ein kooperatives Spiel mit klassischem Fantasysetting. Die Spieler verkörpern die Rolle von Fantasyhelden, dabei werden die genretypischen Klischees bedient: Zwerg, Krieger, Magier und Bogescnhütze stehen zur Auswahl Die Erweiterung "Neue Helden", sei hier direkt Denjenigen ans Herz gelegt, die mehr Abwechslung bei der Heldenauswahl haben möchte. Nachdem jeder Spieler einen Helden ausgewählt hat, geht es mit dem Einführungsspiel los und man lernt die grundlegenden Mechaniken kennen. An dieser Stelle sei direkt die Anleitung kritisiert: Diese ist so auf den schnellen und unkomplizierten Start ausgelegt, dass es durchaus offene Fragen gibt. Die Mechaniken von Andor sind gut durchdacht und greifen sinnig ineinander. Dabei ist es für die Helden wahrlich kein Zuckerschlecken das Zielzu erreichen. Der Schwierigkeitsgrad ist durchaus knackig und die Aktionen derHelden wollen gut überlegt sein. Natürlich spielt auch das Glück eine sehr große Rolle, denn wenn die Würfel beim heldenangriff partout nur wenig Augen zeigen wollen, rückt der Sieg in weite Ferne. Die Szenarien und die gesamte Geschichte werden dabei stimmungsvoll erzählt und schaffen eine tolle Atmosphäre. Als Fan von kooperativen Spielen, sollte man Andor mal gespielt haben.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
In this 2-4 player cooperative dungeon crawl game, players take on a particular scenario, trying to prevent monsters from overrunning their castle, and meeting the victory conditions. The players slowly learn about the requirements of what they have to do as the game evolves.

Players have seven hours in a day, in which 1 hour represents 1 movement point which they can use to move and fight. Players can gain strength and other items by trading in gold. Players can earn willpower (represents how many dice you roll in combat) and gold by defeating monsters, but each monster you defeat shortens the game by one turn. The combat is fairly streamlined, and you can get dice bonuses with helms or witches brew. 

It's a refreshing game in the sense that the quest you play will be new the first time you play it. It's really fun and really makes you work together. I'm looking forward to more plays. 
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

RATING: N/A
This is the first game we bought without months of research, watching playthroughs, reading reviews... Zeynep chose this game by purely looking at the back of the box, reading the text there, and because there was a 20% off all games at the store, we went for it. And good thing we did, this game is really good! First off the board is the best I've seen in any game, the artwork is brilliant. The gameplay is good, I've read a lot of complaints about the passing of time after an enemy is defeated. I think it makes sense both thematically and mechanically. Technically, if you waste your time fighting monsters instead of doing objectives, of course you're gonna be set back a day. Well, maybe not a full day, but that's where the gameplay aspect comes into play. The players are expected to secure the castle, and accomplish given objectives at the same time. I think the intent is to avoid players just clearing the entire board and only then going for the objectives. The players need to make sure they secured the castle just enough that they can venture off and come back to defend again. There are more legends on the website including a solitaire one. Overall, a big thumbs up.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7.2
Even if the theme might lead to think so, this is not a hack n' slash ameritrash game where you have trash your enemies, this game is more like a puzzle. You need quite thorough strategic consideration in order to accomplish the legends, otherwise you will fail for sure.

The learning process is a bit annoying for those veteran gamers like me who are used to read the manuals and don't feel confortable starting to play without knowing how to play... But it works.


What I like:
·) Very original and clever mechanics; different from every other game.
·) The games are tense, the Legends are well designed, there's a sensation of continuity and progress in each of them, you do things and you see how things advance. You don't get bored!
·) The graphic design is superb, a proud work of Michael Menzel. Still, the game would feel better with plastic miniatures at least for the players.
·) I don't know why, but I don't see a very intense "leader effect" in this coop game. 


What I don't like:
·) Lack of replayability. Yes, there are different cards and setups that provide different games, but the overall strategy and the experience is more or less the same. So is the feeling. When I repeat the Legends after a failed mission, they feel the same even if the setup and random events are different. Once you "solve the puzzle", it doesn't make a lot of sense to "solve" it again.
·) There are setups that combined with the random events, make 100% impossible to win. You don't know at the beginning and maybe you don't realize when it happens, but it's certainly there.


This game is really an 8, but the lack of replayability leaves it with a 7.2.

RATING: 9
First of all the artwork is lovely and it's one of the games that is very story-driven and you can really become immersed into the world. 
The characters really have their different strengths, which is nice, because you really have to plan not only what to do, but also who is best suited to do it. 
It's extremly tough in the beginning maybe even a little too much, but after a few more plays I enjoy the fact that it actually is. 
The introduction to it is pretty great, because it is a little bit videogameish and you can introduce people to it that way, which normally would be put of by the complexity that it looks to be like, when seeing all the components. 

The original legends become a little too repetitive after a while, but the expansion helps with that and as with many story-driven games it often just helps to set it aside for a while and then replay it again after a while, when the stories are not so "fresh" in mind anymore.

RATING: 5
First impressions: 

Beaten-to-death fantasy setting with stereotype characters and a standard "first move, then encounter" design, and dull combat system. I'd appreciate the story telling element, if the story itself just wasn't so worn off.

The game seems thematic, of course, yet some mechanisms are Euro-ish in the worst of ways, like, for example, the storyteller proceeding with each defeated monster. I hate these kind of unthematic rules in a thematic game.

I suppose replayability is very low.

*此遊戲第一關是介紹任務有特殊設置，之後基本設置如下
*根據卡片做基本設置，河邊的圓格隨機蓋著放15個霧版塊，準備對應的劇情卡照字母疊起，使用金色的事件卡放一旁，白色標記放右邊回合軌第一格，井蓋著放對應位置，事件卡上有的字母在回合軌上放星號標記做提醒，紅色方塊圓片跟骰放下放，裝備放在裝備版上，之後根據劇本的A卡設置目標跟怪物
*每個玩家拿一個腳色，起始力量一放方塊，血量七放圓片，再放一個圓片到右上時間軌起始格，腳色根據起始地點位置放置，腳色能力看腳色版，物品跟裝備有對應格上限，錢跟寶石無上限
*遊戲進行多個回合，回合由起始玩家開始順時針進行，每次腳色行動4選一，直到所有腳色跳過進入日落階段，正常每個英雄有7個時間，每多花兩血可多一個，最多三個，要再回合軌到達N之前完成劇本任務，否則也算輸
1.移動 可移動任意相鄰格，每走一格左上時間軌右移一格，停留點有效果結算不花行動，可跟怪物同格，河流不能通過，過橋的橋本身不花時間
*霧版塊一定要翻面結算，井就補三滴之後翻面，寶石或錢或物品就拿，跟其他人同格可以交換，商人格可以花兩圓買1力量或物品
*使用物品 
>威士忌可以使用兩次，第一次翻面，用完丟回裝備版，可不花時間移動一格
>盾牌也可以使用兩次，可幫自己檔一次傷害，或避免負面事件(左下有盾牌符號的)
>有弓則可相鄰攻擊，丟骰規則同射手，同格不能使用弓
>頭盔可讓你結算時加總同骰點的骰
>望遠鏡只能在停在地點時使用，可開所有相鄰的版塊
>老鷹 有老鷹個可以跟任意位置英雄交換小物件(頭盔，藥水都算)，一回合一次，使用翻面，下一回合翻回
>女巫藥水 一次戰鬥輪使用一次，最多兩次後丟回，可將一骰點兩倍，只能用在自己的，無法跟頭盔連動
>草藥 使用後可移動不花時間，或是補血或是戰鬥丟完骰加攻擊力(怪丟骰前)，使用藥草上的數值加強，不管使用多少都要丟掉
>符文石 英雄可選擇不打開拿，如果他三種顏色都有則獲得一顆黑骰來取代一顆平常丟的骰
2.等待 不動單純花一個時間
3.跳過 把時間標記放回起始格，最先回去的放在公雞格，成為下回合起始
4.戰鬥 分成多個回合直到結束條件，每次花一個時間，英雄根據規則丟骰，選骰值最高的加上戰力扣掉怪物丟骰跟怪物戰力和(怪物如果兩骰相同則加總，否則取高)，扣到對應的腳色血量上，如果沒結束就在花一個時間繼續直到結束條件，打贏時根據怪物拿獎勵(血跟錢可任意比例拿)，且怪物放到右下80區回合軌前進一格(有觸發劇情就要念卡結算)，如果英雄沒血就掉一力量，回三血，如果玩家沒時間或取消戰鬥，則怪物血回滿
*戰鬥時如果弓箭手相鄰，或是有其他英雄同格可一起戰鬥，戰力加總之後再照順位丟骰(觸發戰鬥的先)，所有英雄的各自最高骰點加總，每次戰鬥所有英雄都要花一個時間，戰勝獎勵要平均平分，如果輸則所有英雄都要扣差值血量(巫師的效果要在該玩家丟完骰就決定，不能等全部)，戰鬥可在中途退出但就不能再加入
*如果要使用女巫藥水或是草藥要在自己丟完骰就用，不能等怪丟骰
*日落階段 
>抽一張事件結算
>移動小怪 從數字小到大的區域每個怪照箭頭移動到相鄰格，如果目標地點已經有怪則在照箭頭移動到沒怪的地方
>根據順位移動剩下的怪，規則同上
*如果怪物走到城堡就放到城堡旁空格，根據人數如果空格不夠放就輸了
>所有沒有英雄的井翻面
>回合標記上升一格，如果有對應標記就讀劇情卡
*遊戲在開劇情卡如果有綠色的時候可以選擇讀綠色來玩簡單模式
*遊戲其他腳色或地點
>巫女 藏在霧中，當遇到可以馬上免費拿到一個巫師藥水，之後可買根據人數價格不同，弓箭手都少花一元
>農夫 每個被帶進城堡的農夫，可以增加城堡的怪物上限一，英雄同格時就可以帶著一起走，也可不要，只要經過就可以帶，怪物只要一跟農夫同格農夫就移除
>王子跟矮人護衛 同格時戰力+4，多一個可選行動為花一個時間移動此標記四格(可多次)
>石頭 任何單位都不能跨越，相鄰英雄可使用戰鬥來移除，花一個時間，多個可一次移除，也可多個英雄一起
>寶石 寶石數值可當錢使用，第五章例外，如果怪物相鄰寶石，則移動時會移動過去並移除寶石，選價值高的先

RATING: 7

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
Defined scenarios that may be too fixed to warrant a lot of replay - that's the big fear, that there's not enough randomness within each scenario to warrant replay once it's been done and dusted, especially if you beat it first turn. Nonetheless it's a big hit with my tween boys because of the great art and the simple rule set. You've got seven actions each day (before the baddies move closer), use them to move a space or to fight, trying to beat up the baddies before they get to the Castle, in a homage to Castle Panic. The combat is fun enough though - each player is given a different dice process - and you can use the gold won by beating up the small baddies to buy stuff to boost you for the fights against the medium and big baddies. For those, you need to organise yourselves and take them on as teams, combining your combat values - and that's the essence of the co-op here. There's not lots of hard decisions - it's more about admiring the story, going along for the ride, rolling some dice and coming out on top. 
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 9
"Gorgeous, puzzle-like, rich-storied, fantasy adventure co-op. Hooray for the hero gender options! My wife thinks the game feels quite punishing, and she prefers lighter games, so she doesn't like it  as much as I do. The setup is just daunting at first, but becomes quick. Legend 3 is very replayable."

What I like:
- Very beautiful art AND functional layout
- Tutorial was a fun way to learn together
- Very thematic, and I love how the story unfolds
- Love the scenario system
- Legend 3 is as replayable as any standard co-op
- Gender choices for the heroes

What I don't like:
- A couple rules are vague and/or easy to overlook
- First plays of legends 1 and 2 make it seem like there is no way to ever win (but they are winnable)
- Can be like solving a group puzzle, with possible alpha player issues
- The tutorial can make you feel like you don't quite know enough, even though you do
- The official solo variant is OK, but not great

This is a really interesting design, and I am enjoying exploring the full world of Andor. I would put the weight around 2.8. It took us 90 minutes from opening the box to finishing scenario #1 (with a narrow loss).

Don't judge the game until you have played Legend 3 a couple times. The other legends are like video game puzzles that you have to play repeatedly to "solve", but Legend 3 has as much variability as a standard co-op game, so is fully replayable. 

I'm not a big solo player, but I have played legend 3 about 10 times solo so far (including with the new heroes expansion). I don't like controlling multiple heroes in a game, but this one is best with 3, good with 2 or 4, and just OK with 1. It's fun enough that I put up with playing 3 heroes. 

After 21 plays (mostly legend 3), I'm increasing my rating from 8 to 9.

RATING: 7
Just 1 play and it was like a co-operative game should be: you have the idea you can win, but you lose close to the finish. So far, so good. 

This game won a lot of prices and even was the 2013 'Spiel des Jahres -  Kennerspiel des Jahres' Winner. And while I can see this is a good game, I wonder why? I mean, what is really new about it? Scenario's: seen before. Beating up monster to prevent them invading a castle: seen before. Develop your hero to make him stronger: seen before. Do other stuff in the meanwhile: seen before. 

The only really new thing I can think about is that every monster you slash brings you 1 day closer to the end of the game. But is it that that makes it win so many prizes? Off course the nice artwork of Menzel probably works. But what worries me the most about this game is the replayability from just the base game. You probably just have to buy all forecoming expansions to keep this game interesting, because once you've done all existing scenario's (and the base game only has 5 :s), the will be not a lot challenge left.

RATING: 7.3
Legends of Andor might best be described as a cooperative Ameritrash-style tower defense - even though it has scenario driven story points and strong Euro-elements. Players take on the role of characters who represent standard fantasy tropes, the Ranger, the Fighter, Dwarf, & Wizard, each with unique abilities, and strike out into the world to fight the forces of evil. What makes Legends unique is the way in which the enemies act. There is a random element to seeding of the board with enemies at the beginning and sometimes throughout the game, but once the enemies have been placed, their actions are mostly prescribed & predictable. The players, then, are tasked with balancing the enemies' steady advance and the other tasks defined by the scenario.

RATING: 7
A completely co-op race against time puzzle adventure game with dice rolling for combat. While there is luck, there is luck mitigation through getting equipment and leveling your character. Replayabilty in this case would be pretty much only through new adventures, as each game you see pretty much everything a particular adventure has to offer. The game has very easy rules, that are clear and plays very smoothly. While this doesn't come with minis, the cardboard standups are very well done, and my playgroup really appreciates that they included male and female versions of each character.

:star: Art, Iconography and components functional
:star: Clever or interesting mechanisms
:star: Reasonably low downtime between turns with mildly AP players
:star: Multiple plays stay interesting
:nostar: Low or mitigatable luck elements
:star::star::star::nostar::nostar: Raw enjoyment

RATING: N/A

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
A lot of fun. I love a cooperative game that really knows how to lay on the difficulty. The mechanics are simple enough and the tutorial mission make learning the game a breeze. There's plenty of strategy to be discovered through combos of certain items/abilities, though I wonder about the replay value once everything is discovered.

My big complaints about the game:
1. So much production value, especially in the tutorial mission, but I wish the money was spent on nice miniatures instead.
2. Often the mechanics don't synch up with the theme- like being punished for defeating monsters or how the wizard has almost no use for willpower. 
3. The rulebook is basically non-existant. You're taught the game through cards, and it leaves a lot of questions.

Overall: Despite it's obvious flaws, Andor is a game I'll look forward to playing until probability dictates it grows stale.

RATING: 7
2-4p 60-90 min adventure dice rolling gw 2.7 rank 248
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 2
This game plays like a story.  You feel like you are on an epic journey while playing it.  There are several down sides to this game.

First, people pretty much have to play through the scenarios in order.  So, if you are constantly teaching people the game you will be playing the first 2 scenarios over and over and over and over.  This just means you need to find a good gaming group to play it through all the scenarios.

Second, which is totally a personal opinion and easily rectified, is the narrator advancing rule.  Every time you kill an enemy the narrator advances, which puts a time limit of sorts on the game.  We HATED this and decided to instead use a variant as follows:

When defeating a creature roll a red die. Do the following:

1-2: Gain 1/2 reward and the creature respawns
3-4: Gain 1/2 reward and the creature doesn't respawn
5-6: Gain full reward, the creature doesn't respawn and the narrator moves.

Respawn:
Roll a red die and a hero die.
Red Die: 1-2 = 20, 3-4 = 40, 5-6 = 50
Hero Die: = Face Value
Place the monster on the space of the Red Die + Hero Die
(i.e. Red die = 3, Hero die = 4 => Respawn at 44)

We have used this house rule for all but the 4th scenario (the 4th scenario is very different than the rest) and we like what it offers.

Finally, the things you want to do in this game are always out of reach.  For this reason I will never play it again with the rules as they are.  The basic game mechanics are really cool - monster movement, battle mechanics, the scenario cards, etc.  The "fringes" are terrible - buying items (especially from the witch), gaining strength, etc.  Our group NEVER purchased anything from the witch (it's simply too expensive).  Uncovering the fog is so fun, but only one person ever really gets to do it - that sucks!  This game is really tight, which isn't necessarily bad; but it becomes bad when it locks you out of all the cool things you want to do in the game.  This game does exactly that - so it's bad!

Once my game group finished the campaign we sold this game.  I hope to never play another game like this again.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
RPG-Themed Cooperative board game with a wide variety of both characters to play and enemies to kill. Play through the six different Legends, all while "leveling up", looting items, trading gold for items and encountering the many different mechanics used in The Legends of Andor.

Box contains:
- Gear items (shields, helmets, bow and arrow, healing potions, etc
- Figures of 4 heroes to play with (Swordsman, Dwarf, Mage and Archer)
- More than 20 enemy figures (different in size, level and strength)
- An enemy Dragon, which need some slaying in one of the Legends (spoiler alert?)
- "Gold" coins, reward coins and many more
- Deck of cards with random events
- Deck of cards with playthrough mechanic of all Legends
- Huge foldable board with two sided-print (of two different worlds/dungeons!)
And much more...

8/10 - Would definitely play the Legends more than once and would totally recommend it to anyone who is interested in RPG/COOP boardgames

Michael Menzel híresen jó illusztrátor a játékvilágban - első saját játékában pedig nem fukarkodott. Minden komponens szemrevaló, csak az üres táblát el tudom nézegetni 10 percig. RATING: 8.2
Impressed by the introduction mission alone. Looking into the box, still filled with many components not explained in the basic intro, I realised this was just the tip of a massive iceberg filled with beautiful, fantasy adventure.

Coop is a pet peeve of us, and the game engine is tough. Haven't yet mastered the intro-game. The stuff yet to discover in this box has me wanting to go back to the lands of Andor for more. I'm looking forward to gear up my hero and travel far and wide into this magic land. I'm really excited to return and unfold the stories in the Legends! 

Edit: finished legend 2 and I can safely say, this is a great game!

RATING: 9


Recently won the "Kennerspiel des Jahres" 2013, well deserved.

Fantastic experience, easy to get into, no work or preparation, only simple fun. Coop fantasy game with top notch art and easy, fast play. One of the best new FFG game of the last years along with Netrunner. Strongly recomend it for a quick and easy fantasy fix.

Don't mind those negatives comments in the recent threads, those guys didn't get the spirit of the game. Comments about lack of replay value and the fact of the combat advanced the time marker being antithematic are clearly wrong or derived from a wrong expectation by the players. Believe me, the game is awesome, full of adventure. 

There is a ton of 'replayability' (at least for me) and the combat and time mechanic is great and completely thematic. It goes along with a 'tower defense' engine where you have to pick the right fights and get the job done before your time runs out.

RATING: 7.3
It's a comparatively simple, fully cooperative adventure game. The biggest strength of this title is probably the tutorial, which is integrated into the first scenario.

Very few rules have to be read before starting your first game, which probably makes this a very good gateway game for cooperative board games. Basically that's the same 'niche' filled by Pandemic (another simplistic coop-board-game with little to offer for board-gamers who are already familiar with modern games and willing to read rules) and takes slightly longer to play, but in my opinion decisions are more meaningful and the theme is vastly more attractive in this one, which is why I rated it higher than Pandemic.

Note that, IF you are looking for a game to introduce someone to modern board games, this might easily one of the very best games you could get. In that case: Ignore the rating and just get this!
