RATING: 4
The theory of the game is good, however, there is only 1 way to play each scenario, if you mess 1 thing up you lose, which sucks with how long the game can take. Impossible to win with less than 4 players. Since it is chance/dice roll based battles, you need to boost your chances in rolling better than the enemies, which can be done with upgrades and grinding, however, each time you beat an enemy you move the timeline. Beat too many enemies defend or upgrading, you lose!! Defend your base by defeating enemies, you lose!! Phase timeline moves by default after everyone is out of moves. Can be improved and made enjoyable by one simple change, don't move endgame timer after every enemy kill. Changes game completely to a more RPG adventure, can upgrade, grind, explore, without having to plan every step from move 1.

RATING: 5.25
Beautiful artwork, particularly the main board. Enjoy the learn as you go approach. However, translation and implementation issues make navigating the rules frustrating. Very thematic with highly complementary mechansisms(time track and puzzly prioritization). That said, this game rubs us the wrong way. We've found the mix of luck (dice-driven combat resolution), limited resources (time), and determinism (set story events) to conflict. There's very little margin for error and the game is lengthy, so luck doesn't have a place here. For example, one bad roll early on can lose you the game 30-40 minutes later. As a result, the game is less than the sum of its parts.

Menzel játéka lehet a legjobb időben talált rám. Hihetetlen, hogy 2 oldal jól érthető szabály után már játszható a játék. 4 oldal szabály után már az első kalandon is túl vagyunk. Nagyon jól kitalált a mesébe bevezetés. Lehet családoknak, kezdő társasoknak még így sem lesz rögtön minden kristálytiszta, de gyakorlottabbaknak nem jelent akadályt. Az elsőt éppen megcsináltuk, a másodikat éppen elbuktuk. A játékot ostorozók az újrajátszhatóságát kérdőjelezik meg. Jogosan, bár én egyáltalán nem éreztem ezt két játék után. Igen, vannak sarokpontok és trükkök, amikkel egy-egy legenda könnyebben megoldható, de bőven van random tényező, ami szerintem többször újrajátszhatóvá teszi a játékot. Biztos vagyok benne, hogy sok nagynevű játéknál többször kerülne elő egy közepesen erős gémer csapatnál. A játékidő is jól eltalált. A rettentő hosszú ameritrash játékokhoz képest, itt 1,5 óra alatt lejászható volt 1-1 legenda. Aki szereti a fantasyt annak szerintem mindenképpen érdemes megnézni és kipróbálni. =-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
This is an interesting game.  It is a story-driven cooperative adventure game with a fantasy setting.  The gameplay is very simple but I'm actually okay with that part because the focus of the game is on the story and that really does manage to flesh it out the rest of the way for me.

One major complaint that a fellow gamer has levied upon this game (and games like it such as Mice and Mystics) is that the story progression is very arbitrary.  And it is, the story progresses at the end of every day and also whenever a monster is defeated in battle.  I don't, however, feel this takes too much away from the game.

In my one play of the game so far the difficulty and game tempo seemed to be pretty perfectly balanced is why.  At first I worried that we accelerated the story too much by advancing it after every successful battle but everything fell into place in our first game pretty well (the introductory campaign).

That said I have a HUGE problem with the amount of content that comes with this game.  There are only 6 adventures and really there are only 4.  The first is introductory and meant to introduce the major elements of the game without really giving you the whole experience and the 6th is a cop-out set of blank cards for writing your own adventure.  I'm not that creative and even if I were I don't really want to take the time to do the designer's job.

4 plays is not a lot of mileage to get out of the retail price of a game and judging from my first play I'm sure repeat plays will not be as interesting.

In the end it is a coop game that plays really easily for families and a wide array of gamer levels and plays a little differently than other coops I have so I'm not too disappointed with it.  It's simplicity combined with its lack of replayability do keep it from shining too bright though.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 3
Terribly boring puzzle.  Even fans will admit that there's basically one solution to the problem, which means it is completely a take it or leave it kind of game.  The killing monsters means you have less time to win mechanic is completely silly.  It makes very little sense even if you try to argue that you shouldn't waste time killing monsters because monsters are always moving toward the castle.  If some monsters moved off in a random direction and really were inconsequential to kill, I could stomach it.

But therein lies the heart of the problem.  The game is like a trial and error NES game.  Once you know what to do, the only challenge left is whether or not you can actually press the buttons (or in this case, roll the dice well) fast enough.  This means that games literally come entirely down to luck once you happen upon the solution.  This is vastly irritating.  It also means that if you didn't happen upon the solution, you are basically guaranteed to lose.  That's infuriating.  I realize some people like this style of gameplay, but there's a reason modern games moved away from such trial and error gameplay.

RATING: 3
I had such high hopes for this game. The components are nice, the art is nice, they actually give you an even gender mix of characters and the women look like real adventurers.
The game is well set up to learn, with an intro that gets you straight into the game. I dread the thought of having to look up rules later with this setup however - there's no real "rulebook" at all.
The action mechanics, leveling up and fighting monsters are all decent.
All of which is ruined for me by one mechanic I completely despise. You are under a time limit to complete scenarios. Defeating monsters pushes the timer forward. You are punished for doing what you MUST do to defend the castle! It makes no thematic sense, and leads to incredibly frustrating game that just "feels" wrong. (We have been winning scenarios by the way - this is no way reduces the intense frustration). Most of the game is geared toward fighting monsters, yet you aren't allowed to fight monsters!
I managed to get over this for scenario 3, and was trying to accept it, and then we hit "draw a card and you lose because you upgraded too much" which you never could have known would be a problem. I despise trial-and-error gameplay, and this is trial-and-error at its worst.
+co-op+

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
This is a cooperative adventure game.  Play one of 4 different characters and try to complete the quest while preventing the castle from being overrun.

There are 4 different scenarios.  The storyline of each scenario is played out by drawing cards from a predetermined deck of cards.  Players take turns using their actions.  Depending on what you do, you spend a certain amount of time.  You can do more time consuming actions on your turn and that is made up by other players able to take enough actions to catch up in time.

Dice is rolled to fight monsters.  The way you determine success is different depending on your class.  You can obtain treasure to increase your abilities throughout the course of your quest.

There is no actual rule book that describes how to play this game.  The manuals make you play out the introductory quest to learn how to play the game.  Each part of the introductory quests teaches you one aspect of the game.  I would have liked a manual to teach the game and make the introductory quest optional.  It would make it easier to teach new players if not everyone in the group is a new player.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 9
Rated this game as a family/kids game (age 8-10). Kept everyone engaged, even my younger kids wanted to be present and roll the dice.

My eldest kept asking for it, getting other kids at our vacation spot to play it as well.

Highly recommended for the gamer dads/gamer mothers amongst us!

As for the game itself: mechanically it is a simple puzzle optimization (feels akin to Mage Knight light), however the thematics in this game are strong and the illustrations really draw you in. This is probably what makes it such an excellent light family game: mechanically easy enough to be grasped by children aged 8-10, while visually engaging enough to draw (and hold) everyone's attention.

Eat your heart out, Defenders of the Realm.

Without kids: too light and dry for my taste, despite the gorgeous artwork. Too much alpha problem as it is a puzzle coop. Drop rating by 2 points: still a fine game but certainly not one I'll suggest on a game night.

[APR 2017] This game is requested over and over by my kids. They really dig it so that's why I keep it around. As for myself, because this can be pretty unforgiving game making the bad decisions I find myself making all the decisions and getting myself a headache by doing it. Basically, not my game of choice but the excitement of the kids is what matters. Played when my youngest want to join his elder brother and friends in some epic monster slaying. Stashed away otherwise, awaiting the time my kids lose interest.

RATING: 7.2
OK, I guess most of you know by now that I'm not a big fan of co-op games. I like the idea, but I'm still hoping that one will turn up that I really love.
OK, so on to this game. Respectable publisher, respectable artist, first time designer. That could be a winner of course. And I guess most people will see it as a winner. This is one fine designed game. But it didn't blow me away and it didn't feel all that original. It was touted as being a quite original take on the co-op genre, but it didn't feel like that to me.
We skipped the intro scenario and moved on to the next one right away. It proved a good move as this was a challenging scenario for first time players that we only lost barely.
So all in all I found this to be a very solid game, but it is not as original as I expected and it didn't do anything that changes my stance on co-ops.

RATING: 5.5
There are a lot of weird things about the game that seem very unpolished or unconventional.  The cardboard standees, the names of all the monsters, and the names of the heroes in particular are just kind of odd.  It's also strange that you somewhat get punished for killing enemies because it pushes you closer to running out of time.  But all that said, I've enjoyed my first two plays.  The leveling up aspect is kind of lacking, but there is some power growth.  Combat is fairly simple yet somehow very satisfying.  The missions are interesting and really force you to not waste any time.  Both missions so far have come down to the wire with one win and one loss.

Update: After 5 plays I decided to let this go.  The stories were thin and the missions felt like bland optimization combined with swingy dice chucking.

RATING: 8
Played the first two introductory quests. Nice coop, and I like the way the rules are introduced gradually. Of course, it has a lot in common with other coops. Go somewhere, keep the threats in check, solve the task and balance all the activities you have and want to do. Not sure about replayability . do you need a new scenario when you play, or can you retry the same challenge more than a few times?

--

After more plays I can see some replayability. The game can be a brain burner, especially on the last few turns. How many monsters can we kill, and how many do we have to kill until one of the end game conditions kicks in? How much strength do we need to kill this enemy? Can we still pick up that object before we must face this threat? Who should start the battle, and can we stilkl make it when we wait for the last player character to arrive? T-hese questions involve a lot of counting spaces and adding numbers, so if you do not like this, stay away from Andor. This is a themed Euro-Coop, not Ameritrash.

RATING: 6
An streamlined fantasy co-op.

This game has both a great theme and some very decent mechanics. It works great, and can easily be played by new gamers (which is not the case with most if not all fantasy adventure games of this scale). Luck is only a randomiser in this game, and player actions/cooperation win or lose a game. It flows exremelly well and provides some pretty satisfying gameplay experience.

I've played the first 4 scenarios so far and I dare say replayability may be an issue. Out of all 4 only the 3rd is really replayable and that was too easy in our first play. There is a way to rump up difficulty but I see little reason to do so as it really is arbitary - just less "time" to complete that legend. The second problem I have with this game is the legend track. In all the thematic games I've played I've found some way to translate mechanics into theme - some are ridiculous and maybe laughable but they at least make the mechanics accepted and less arbitary. The legend track in this game has beaten my imagination. Half the time it advances when a day passes and half the time when a monster is killed. I can see it works brilliantly mechanics wise for the game, but I just can't explain it thematically and it bothers me. If the mechanics are the bones of a game and the theme the skin and flesh then there is nothing covering the legend track in this game - it's just bones.

Overall I think this is a brilliant game with two nearly fatal flaws. Some may ignore them, others may consider them trivial but for now I'd rather play some more before I finally make my mind.

RATING: 6.5
I picked up this game in a math trade to play with my son. It's just the sort of game he likes, a cooperative game set in a D&D-ish theme. For our initial play, we played a two player run through of the introductory Legend One.

For those who don't know the game, the first mission, or legend, is just a "Let's teach the new players how the game works" type of thing. So while my initial impression of the game is fairly good, I'm basing that in part on the belief that the other missions will be more fun once the handholding you through how the game works stuff is taken out.

I enjoyed the initial mission. It gave a pretty good idea how the game will play with the standard missions. It looks like it will end up being a challenging co-op, with tough choices.

I have a little concern that the game only comes with five missions, one of which is never going to be replayed once you learn the game. I've also heard there are some "spoilers" so that also cuts down on the replayability... although I've been assured that the third mission in particular has random elements and provides a lot of opportunity for replay value.

I'll probably update this entry once I have a chance to play the game again. It's a little early to come out definitively on this game.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
[thing=127398][/thing] is a light cooperative game with the focus being on theme, not on mechanics. This doesn't mean that the game has poor rules, just that they don't matter all that much, and you can learn them little by little - the game is designed to do this: in the first scenario, you will learn about movement, exploration and using locations; in the second, about fight, the progress of the story in the scenario, the movement of the monsters. Basically, in this sense, [thing=127398][/thing] is a lighter version of [thing=73171][/thing].

The setting is the realm of normal fantasy: warriors, wizards, castles, monsters, dwarfs (and, as is old D&D, the name serves both as race and class - not sure how the dwarfs fell about this). The scenarios are story-driven and the heroes are different (in powers and in story) from each other. The art is really well done and thematic as it should be: they are truly the vision of the designer, since, well, the designer is also the artist.

The game bits are good, but not as much as in [thing=65532][/thing]: the player boards aren't sturdy, nor the game comes with miniatures - for the heroes and monsters the game uses cardboard pieces, which I don't mind because the art in them is good and is the same thing that I had with [thing=15987][/thing], but with better bases.

I liked the game, but, so far, it hasn't posed a challenge yet. I need challenge in my cooperative plays. Though, it is said that some of the scenarios can be really challenging. I don't know if this means "harder than the usual scenario of this" or "at least as hard as to win a game of [thing=38506][/thing]". I guess is the former - I'm interested enough, anyway, to try and discover.

*******

Addition 07/31/13: I did manage to squeeze a game of the second scenario - [i]Long Live the King[/i] - on sunday, and this scenario really put up a fight to be beaten. We had to think about movement (of our heroes and the monsters) in order to deal with the four demands of the scenario (defend the castle, find the Witch, bring the herbs and destroy the Skrall fortress). I won't rise the grade of [thing=127398][/thing], but I can see that, if the next scenarios are at least as difficult as this last one, I might bump the rate to 8.

RATING: 7
Rating based on playing the first two legends, which we ended with a very close victory. I am not a big fan of co-ops, but Legends Of Andor is a breath of fresh air in the genre - just like Pandemic was in the day. When compared to most american co-ops, Andor feels less random and has more of an emphasis on teamplay. The way each scenario plays is very story-driven - almost like Mice & Mystics. Finally, it plays more like a family game than a gamers' game (just like the titles mentioned previously). All in all, it is a game that I have to be in the mood for, but would love to play every now and then. The artwork by Menzel really adds tons of atmosphere.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 4.5
Initial impression, limited plays.  

Seems like a puzzle with randomness (that could guarantee a loss even with "the/a solution").  The scripting of the game (where enemies appear, where they move is all mostly static) is such that it narrows the solution set to such an extent as to make good play just as scripted.  Worse still, there are events (that are mostly static: e.g. this monster appears at this spot on the board, this other monster appears at this other spot on the board, etc.) which are not supposed to be revealed until later in the game and are necessary information to determining the viable solution(s), virtually guaranteeing a loss the first play through.   

Having only played 2 out of the 5 "Legends" (scenarios) that come with the game (there is another official "Legend" available for free download already); it seems like the game will be too scripted and puzzle like for fans of the adventuring genre (even those that generally like co-ops): while being to random, with far too limited replayability, for those that enjoy the puzzle aspect.  

Most co-ops, especially better (in my - probably not humble enough - opinion) co-ops, such as Arkham Horror, Sentinels of the Multiverse, Pandemic, etc. have game AI which forces players to react to it; Legends of Andor seems to want the players to develop a script and then execute that script against the game's script, with any risk mitigation or backup plans factored into the player's script before the game starts.  

One of the aspects of the game which drives or at least factors into the puzzle aspect of the game is that successfully fighting and defeating an enemy pushes the timer forward (essentially forcing all the heroes to lose a day's worth of actions - 7 actions per hero [ each hero may spend health to get up to 3 more]).  This is: 
1) Not just anti-thematic, but actually draws players out of the theme and forces the puzzle aspect of the game in their face 
2) Extremely counter-intuitive - I just eliminated some of the enemy's forces/resources, so now I have less time to accomplish my goals? 
3) Seems to detract from the purportedly heroic nature of the game/theme (we need to allow as many monsters as possible into the castle so that we don't spend time fighting them) 
4) Just generally seems to negatively impact the fun of playing

Replayability seems low. 
Scaling for number of players seems poor.

RATING: 8
Simple rules, difficult and meaningful decisions, and potentially different every play. Wow! Unlike any dungeon romper I've ever played. Not a kid's adventure game or just a storytelling game - it's a strategy game/RPG hybrid! This feels tense, rather than a pointless hack, grab and slash, ad infinitum. Outstanding (*except that Legends can be won or lost, on the luck of a few bad die rolls)! *Also, docked a point (for difficulty level out of the box), and the need for house ruling (and all that errata).  

I'm quite happy with the standees - my Pathfinder pawns just got a new lease - tabletop RPG style games bore the hell out of me anyway. See below (& *above):

If you're the type that requires your adventurers kill everything in sight, whilst gathering up every available resource by the ton, (kill all - take all - sell off) this probably isn't your style of adventure game. *Detractors stating "it has low re-playability", need to engage their imaginations (or P&P skills). This is HeroQuest on Euro-Steroids!! An game of Euro Quest, anyone? *puff puff* Oh, official re-playability. See below:

*There's hope some great expansions are forthcoming (especially, for the reverse side of that breathtaking board).. and please, please, make an ADVENTURE KIT (someone) to ease creating new scenarios... for the PC... someone/anyone - Hint hint... RATING: 7
This great theme, strategy, and characters.  The board and chits are beautiful.  The characters all feel different and have unique abilities.  You really feel like you're in the realm of Andor.

Negatives:
the numbering on the board makes it hard to find spaces
takes a while to set up
not much in the way of replayability on certain legends.  

Hack and slash and dungeon crawl lovers be aware, you cannot just kill everything in sight.  Killing a monster has some consequences on time.  You must pick and choose your battles wisely, this to me is a plus.  It creates a lot of thinking, strategy, and tension.

Overall well done solo and coop game.

RATING: 9.1
CAN'T EARN PERMANENT PLACE IN COLLECTION UNLESS THEY PRINT EXPANSIONS IN ENGLISH

What fun! A game with no rulebook that you have to slog through before you begin, and where you learn your objectives as you go along. Great fun! The components are beautiful and clearly presented, and the game - innovatively - prioritises teamwork over monster megadeath. A euro dungeon crawl - would you believe it?!

UPDATE: After 3 plays, each quest can be played several times, even after it's been won since the board state is slightly different with each play. In the medium-term, it's got more than 5 plays in it... I've given it several % extra for including a) female characters and b) female characters in reasonable costumes. This is A BIG DEAL for female gamers. Thank you Michael Menzel - you are a star!

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
Очень красивая кооперативная игра, с простой но занятной механикой. Подходит для семейного времяпрепровождения. легко играется как в компании так и в соло. Представляет по сути игру головоломку. Не является RPG, хотя и очень на него похожа (оформление, тематика и присутствие некоторых RPG элементов). Имеет ограниченное количество официальных сценариев (задачек), хотя они внутр себя имеют рандомизирующий механизм, меняющий различные условия по ходу партии. Есть простор для творчества и написания собственных сценариев, благо дизайн игры дает широкие возможности для построение своих уникальных задачек. Правила достаточно просты. Оформление прекрасное. Хоть все жетоны и картонные, выглядит игра отлично. Партии не очень длинные 1-2 часа. Если вы любите соревноваться, любите глубокие ролевые игры или ваша компания страдает от синдрома - "один игрок решает за всех", то игра скорее всего разочарует. Если нравится кооперативные игры и вы любите совместно решать головоломки, а потом следовать выработанному решению, с поправкой на случайные события, то игра может вам понравится.

RATING: 6
Nicely put together and quite simple co-operative adventure game. The scenario we played was very balanced and it came down to the wire. I liked how indiscriminate combat is discouraged because the time track is advanced for every monster you kill, giving you less time to complete the scenario. That made the game feel different from other dungeon-hack adventures. Streamlined rules, plenty of variability and family-friendliness make this a great mass-market adventure game.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
Theme/Art:
The Art is great, but the theme and setting are a bit too generic for my taste. It's classic mainstream fantasy and it does that very good, but I would have liked some unconventional things.

Production quality:
The design is awesome, but searching for a certain field on the map can be a bit confusing. There are no miniatures, only cardboard figures, but they look really good. There is a LOT of stuff in this game, ranging from cards over tokens for everything and a two-sided board to creatures. Everything feels very high quality.

Replayability:
I haven't played through all the campaigns, but since we lost the first one on our first try and the second one too, I guess it will take some time until we beat the game.
I weight it 3/5.

Depth/Difficulty:
This game has an amazing intro. You don't have to read 50 pages of rules, you simply start a tutorial campaign which explains everything on the go. The game is less complex than it looks, but you have many options to choose from.

Strategy:
You have to work together as a team. Simply doing something and see how it works out will probably lose you the game, you have to consider every step you make and discuss them with your team.

Luck:
Combat is fought via dice rolls, but you can strengthen yourself and group up to make combats as short as possible (short combats are a big part on your way to beat a campaign). There are also event cards, which are drawn from a deck.


A great co-op game, I will update this after I played a few more campaigns.

RATING: 6.7
At first we were fooled into thinking this was a high fantasy romp. It actually plays like a time management, action economy type of affair with a smattering of dice and card flips for random events. The jury is still out for me on this one, I think I may come to appreciate it more once I understand the mind set that the game rewards.

I'm thinking about giving all the scenarios a try then moving this one along.

Along came Gloomhaven and I no longer want to play Legends of Andor!

Tried it again with selling in mind, liked the 2nd scenario enough to keep hold of this and play it some more. The introductory scenario is a poor start to the game, I have the feeling it is going to improve.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 9.55
Very awesome and really challenging game.

The trade-off between killing the monsters and letting them approach and maybe even storm the castle is great too. In other games you just run in and kill all the monsters near you, in Andor every monsters brings you a step closer to losing, this makes the game a fantastic puzzle coop.

For people that never played Legends of Andor before: The tutorial (Legend 1) seems a bit boring at first but is pretty great. All the rules are explained step by step, so it's really easy to learn the game. I was also pretty glad that I didn't have to learn all the rules and then need half an hour to explain them. I'm often the one that reads the rules in advance and learns them to explain the game, so this game was an awesome exception!

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
Why I bought this game:
I was looking for a lightweight alternative to more traditional D&D tabletop RPG experiences that would work for 2 players and would be something my wife and I both enjoyed.

Experience:
We really enjoyed working through the 6 campaigns this game comes with, and completed them over the course of 8 days or so. With only 2 players, the game was enjoyably difficult and required enough strategy to keep us both engaged as we played through each campaign. The mechanics of the game are also enjoyable, mixing event cards, equipment tiles, and dice rolling quite well. We haven't played with any more players yet, but look forward to seeing how the game scales.

Pros:
- Beautiful artwork and gameboard
- Fun campaigns
- Enjoyable cooperative play
- Can find additional campaigns online for free

Cons:
- Only 6 campaigns in box set, reducing replay value
- Long setup (10 minutes or so)

Overall:
I enjoy this game and look forward to printing off some of the free campaigns online, as well as trying this game out with more players.

RATING: 8
An interesting game that brings together a lot of different styles of games into a fresh new package. We've got co-op, high fantasy romp, dungeon-delving, American-style dice chucking, European-style action points, elements of pick-up-and-deliver, economy management, exploration. Whew!

I like this one plenty and the other half likes it even more (that's a rarity, by the way). Recommended!
